Parsing Temporal Words in Talaq and Iqrar: The Hanafi Rule
Explaining how 'before' and 'after' modify meaning in talaq and iqrar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi linguistic rule that 'before' and 'after' describe meaning, not grammatical position, to determine the number of divorces or debts in talaq and iqrar.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, temporal words refer to meaning order, not grammar, flipping the expected talaq count.

When a husband says 'You are divorced one, before it one' or 'after it one', the number of divorces that occur depends on how we interpret 'before' and 'after'. Hanafi jurists have a nuanced rule based on linguistic analysis pointing to the meaning behind the words. This lesson dissects that rule and its application in divorce and confession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two constructions
Recognize the two patterns: 'one divorce before it one' and 'one divorce after it one'. Also note the variant without a pronoun: 'one divorce before one'.
The pronoun 'it' refers to the first divorce.
2
Determine the marital status
The rule applies specifically to a non-consummated (ghayr mawtu'a) wife. Verify that the case is set for such a wife.
For a consummated wife, the rule differs: all divorces occur because she does not become irrevocably divorced by the first.
3
Apply the temporal rule
When 'before' or 'after' is attached to a pronoun (like 'it'), it describes the word that follows it in meaning, not grammar. So in 'one divorce before it one', 'before' describes the second 'one', meaning the second divorce preceded the first in time. That makes both divorces occur at the present moment. In 'one divorce after it one', 'after' describes the future second divorce, which is uncertain, so only the first divorce occurs now.
If there is no pronoun (e.g., 'one divorce before one'), the temporal word describes the preceding word, flipping the outcomes.
4
Extend to iqrar
The same rule applies analogously to confession (iqrar) of debt. For example, 'he owes me one dirham before a dirham' yields one dirham; other forms yield two.
The illa (effective cause) is the absence of a complete locus for multiple obligations.
5
Resolve the counterexample
The text notes a grammatical counterexample: 'a man came to me and Zaid before him'. Here 'before' is attached to a pronoun but describes the preceding noun. The Hanafi resolution restricts the rule to cases where 'before' is not followed by a visible noun other than the attached pronoun.
This shows the rule is pragmatic, not absolute, and fits Hanafi tendency to consider context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بحث أسماء الظروف أنت طالق واحدة قبلها واحدة أو بعدها واحدة تكون القبلية أو البعدية صفة لما بعدها في المعنى وإن كانت بحسب التركيب النحوي صفة لما قبلها، فيقع في الأول طلاقان، وفي الثاني طلاق واحد؛ لأن معنى الأول أنت طالق واحدة التي سبقتها واحدة أخرى، فتقعان معا في الحال، ومعنى الثاني: أنت طالق واحدة التي ستجيء بعدها أخرى، فتقع هذه في الحال ولا يعلم ما سيجيء. وإذا لم تقيد كانت صفة لما قبلها أي إذا لم يقيد كل من القبل والبعد بالكناية بأن يقول: أنت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة أو بعد واحدة تكون القبلية والبعدية صفةً لما قبلها، فيقع في الأول طلاق وفي الثاني طلاقان؛ لأن معنى الأول: أنت طالق واحدة التي كانت قبل الواحدة الأخرى تكون إلخ فإن القبلية والبعدية حينئذٍ قائمة بما بعدها، ثم اعلم أن هذه القاعدة منقوضة بنحو: "جاءني رجل وزيد قبله"، فإن القبل ههنا أضيف إلى الضمير مع أنها صفة لما قبلها كذا قال بعض المحشين ملا محمد عرفان الله ويمكن أن يقال: إن هذه القاعدة مقيدة بما إذا كان بعد القبل اسم ظاهر وإن لم يكن القبل مضافًا إليه، وحينئذ فلا نقض. (القمر) طلاق واحد : أي بائن؛ لأن وضع المسألة في الغير الموطوءة. (القمر) فتقعان إلخ لأنه لما قال: "أنت طالق" وقعت طلقة واحدة ولما وصفها بأن قبلها واحدة أخرى، فحكم بوقوع هذه الوحدة الأخرى في الماضي، وإيقاع الطلاق في الماضي إيقاع في الحال فوقعت هذه أيضًا، فصارت مطلقة بطلقتين معا. (القمر) ولا يعلم ما سيجيء هذه مسامحة والأولى أن يقول: إنه لا يقع الطلاق بعد؛ لأنها غير موطوءة، فلا عدة لها، فليس لوقوع الطلاق بعد طلاق . (القمر) كانت إلخ هذه القاعدة منتقضة بنحو: "جاءني رجل قبل زيد غلامه"، فإن القبل ههنا مضاف إلى الظاهر مع أنه صفة لما بعده كذا قال بعض المحشين أي ملا محمد عرفان ، ويمكن أن يقال: إن هذه القاعدة مقيدة بما إذا لم يكن بعد القبل اسم ظاهر سوى المضاف إليه، وحينئذ فلا نقض (القمر) بالكناية بل تقيد كل منهما بالإضافة إلى الاسم الظاهر. (القمر) بأن يقول: أي للزوجة الغير الموطوءة. (القمر) طلاق : أي بائن لكون وضع المسألة في غير الموطوءة. (القمر) طلاق إلخ لأن وضع المسألة في غير المدخول بها، ووجه تقييدها بها أنه في المدخول بها يقع الجميع؛ لأنها لا تبين بالأولى، ولهذا يلزمه درهمان في مثل: له على درهم قبل درهم أو بعد درهم أو قبله درهم أو بعده درهم؛ إذ الدرهم بعد الدرهم يجب دينًا هكذا في "التلويح"، ويعلم من عبارة الكتاب خلاف ذلك، وهو أن في قوله: "له علي درهم قبل درهم يجب درهم واحد، ووجه كل يظهر من قمر الأقمار فانظر ثمه. (السنبلي) بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بحث أسماء الظروف في الحال الآتية فتقع الأولى ولا يعلم حال الآتية، ومعنى الثاني: أنت طالق واحدة التي كانت بعد الواحدة الأخرى الماضية، فتقعان معًا، وهذا كله في الطلاق وأما في الإقرار فيلزم في قوله: له علي درهم واحد قبل در هم درهم واحد وفي الصور الأخر يلزمه درهمان هكذا قالوا.
Explanation of the divisions of the third division: discussion of names of circumstances. 'You are divorced one, before it one or after it one' — 'before' or 'after' is a description of what follows it in meaning although in terms of grammatical structure it is a description of what precedes it. So in the first case two divorces occur, and in the second case one divorce occurs; because the meaning of the first is: you are divorced one that another one preceded, so both occur immediately. The meaning of the second: you are divorced one after which another will come, so this one occurs immediately and what will come is not known. And if it is not restricted, it is a description of what precedes it: i.e. if each of 'before' and 'after' is not restricted by a pronoun such that he says: 'you are divorced one before one or after one', then 'before' and 'after' are descriptions of what precedes them, so in the first case one divorce occurs and in the second two divorces; because the meaning of the first: you are divorced one that was before another one... then the 'before' and 'after' then pertain to what follows them. Know that this rule is contradicted by something like 'a man came to me and Zaid before him', for 'before' here is attached to a pronoun while it is a description of what precedes it—so said some annotators, Mulla Muhammad Irfan Allah. And it can be said that this rule is restricted to when there is a visible noun after 'before' even if 'before' is not attached to it, and then there is no contradiction. (Qamar) 'one divorce': i.e. irrevocable, because the case is set for the non-consummated wife. (Qamar) 'both occur' etc. because when he said 'you are divorced', one divorce occurred; when he described it as being preceded by another one, he ruled that this other one occurred in the past, and effecting divorce in the past is effecting in the present, so this also occurred, making her divorced by two divorces together. (Qamar) 'and what will come is not known' — this is a liberty; it would be better to say that no divorce occurs later because she is not consummated, so she has no waiting period, so there is no place for a divorce after a divorce. (Qamar) 'was' etc. This rule is contradicted by something like 'a man came to me before Zaid's servant', for 'before' here is attached to a visible noun while it is a description of what follows it—so said some annotators, i.e. Mulla Muhammad Irfan. And it can be said that this rule is restricted to when there is no visible noun after 'before' other than the one attached to it, and then there is no contradiction. (Qamar) 'by pronoun' rather both are restricted by addition to a visible noun. (Qamar) 'that he says' i.e. to the non-consummated wife. (Qamar) 'divorce' i.e. irrevocable because the case is set for the non-consummated. (Qamar) 'divorce' etc. because the case is set for the non-consummated, and the reason for restricting it to her is that for the consummated all occur because she is not separated by the first; hence two dirhams are obligatory in cases like 'he owes me one dirham before a dirham or after a dirham or before it a dirham or after it a dirham', because a dirham after a dirham is required as a debt—thus in al-Talwih; and from the wording of the book it appears otherwise, namely that in his saying 'he owes me one dirham before a dirham', one dirham is obligatory—the reasoning for each appears in Qamar al-Aqmar, so see there. (Sanbali) Explanation of the divisions of the third division: discussion of names of circumstances. In the present case, the first occurs and the state of the coming is not known; meaning of the second: you are divorced one that was after another past one, so both occur together. All this in divorce. As for confession, in his statement 'he owes me one dirham before a dirham', one dirham is obligatory; in the other forms two dirhams are obligatory—thus they said.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a parsing exercise from a Hanafi usul work discussing how the words 'qabla' (before) and 'ba'da' (after) function in legal declarations. The author examines two scenarios in talaq: when the wife is non-consummated (ghayr mawtu'a), the repeated word 'before' or 'after' affects the number of divorces that fall. The key rule is that 'before' and 'after' are attributive to what follows them in meaning, even if grammatically they refer to what precedes. In the first construction ('one divorce before it one'), two divorces occur because the past description brings the second into effect immediately. In the second ('one divorce after it one'), only one occurs because the future is uncertain. When the words are not restricted (i.e., not attached to a noun), they describe what precedes, reversing the outcomes. The author notes a potential counterexample from grammar but resolves it by restricting the rule to cases where 'before' is not followed by a visible noun. The same principle applies to iqrar (confession of debt): 'one dirham before a dirham' yields one dirham, while other forms yield two. The discussion highlights Hanafi juristic reasoning (talil) based on the nature of time and effect.

Key Terms
القبلية (al-qabliyya): The attribute of being before something else; in this context, it describes the temporal precedence of one divorce relative to another.
غير الموطوءة (ghayr al-mawtu'a): A wife who has not been consummated (non-consummated); she has no 'iddah and is not a locus for multiple divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Two
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule on temporal words in talaq turns on linguistic meaning, not grammar, and it is restricted to non-consummated wives and analogous in iqrar.

Ghayr as Adjective and Exception in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the dual usage of 'ghayr' as adjective and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ghayr as adjective and ghayr as exception based on case ending, and apply this distinction to Hanafi legal acknowledgments.

Core Idea
Ghayr's case ending decides legal obligation: nominative = adjective, accusative = exception.

The word ghayr is a linguistic tool with two distinct legal functions. In Hanafi usul, the same utterance can yield different rulings depending on how ghayr is inflected. This lesson unpacks that distinction using a classic example from legal acknowledgments, demonstrating how a single word can determine the amount owed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two usages of ghayr
Recognize that ghayr can function as an adjective (sifah) for indefinite nouns or as an exception (istithna). The original usage is adjectival; the exceptive usage is subsidiary.
This duality is a key feature of ghayr in Arabic grammar.
2
Analyze grammatical markers
The case ending of ghayr determines its function: nominative (raf‘) indicates an adjective, accusative (nasb) indicates an exception. This is the primary analytical step.
The case ending is the decisive linguistic evidence.
3
Apply to the dirham-daniq example
Examine the statement: 'He has upon me a dirham other than a daniq.' With nominative, ghayr is an adjective, so a full dirham is owed. With accusative, it is an exception, so only a dirham minus a daniq (five-sixths) is owed.
The practical consequence is a 1/6 difference in debt.
4
Extend to siwa and intention
The word 'siwa' (سوى) functions similarly to ghayr. However, because its declension is estimated (i‘rab taqdiri), interpretation relies on the speaker's intention. The judge may not accept a claim of intended exception if the utterance was defective.
Intention plays a role when grammar is ambiguous.
5
Consider the judge's stance
In cases of lightening (takhfif) – presumably a slip of the tongue – the judge does not accept the speaker's claim that exception was intended. The default is the literal grammatical form.
Establishes a presumption in favor of the apparent grammatical structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بحث "غير" بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث "غير" يستعمل صفة للنكرة، ويستعمل استثناء، لكن الاستعمال الأول أصل فيه، والثاني تبع فهو أيضًا داخل في الظروف تغليبا كقوله : له" على درهم غير دائق بالرفع، فيلزمه در هم تام؛ لأنه حينئذٍ ،صفة للدرهم، فيكون المعنى له علي الدرهم الذي هو مغاير للدائق، فلا يستثنى منه شيء فيلزم درهم تام. ولو قال بالنصب كان استثناء، فيلزمه درهم إلا دانقا وهو مقدار سدس الدرهم، أي بنصب غير الدائق و"سوى" مثل "غير" في كونه صفة واستثناء وهو ظرف في الحقيقة، لكن لما كان إعرابه تقديريًا يحال على النية، ولعل القاضي لا يصدقه في صورة التخفيف.
Discussion of 'ghayr': Explanation of the third division: 'ghayr' is used as an adjective for indefinite nouns, and it is used as an exception. However, the first usage is the original, and the second is subsidiary. It is also included among adverbs by way of predominance, as when he says: 'He has upon me a dirham other than a daniq' with raf', then a complete dirham is obligatory; because then it is an adjective of dirham, so the meaning is: he has upon me the dirham that is other than the daniq, so nothing is excepted and a complete dirham is obligatory. If he said with nasb, it would be an exception, and he would owe a dirham except a daniq, which is one-sixth of a dirham, i.e. with nasb of 'ghayr al-daniq'. And 'siwa' is like 'ghayr' in being an adjective and an exception, and it is actually an adverb, but because its declension is estimated, it is referred to intention, and perhaps the judge does not believe him in the case of lightening.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Noor al-Anwar explains the dual grammatical and legal usage of the word 'غير' (ghayr). The author first states that 'غير' is used both as an adjective (صفة) for indefinite nouns and as an exception (استثناء). The original usage is adjectival; the exceptive usage is subsidiary. Nevertheless, 'غير' is treated as an adverb by predominance. The example given is a legal acknowledgment: if someone says 'he has upon me a dirham other than a daniq' (له علي درهم غير دائق) with the nominative case (رفع) on 'غير', it functions as an adjective, meaning the dirham is described as being different from a daniq. Thus, a full dirham is owed because nothing is excepted. If said with the accusative case (نصب), it functions as an exception, so only a dirham minus a daniq (five-sixths of a dirham) is owed. The word 'سوى' (siwa) is similar, being both adjective and exception, and is actually an adverb. However, because its declension is estimated, its interpretation depends on the intention of the speaker. In the case of lightening (التخفيف) – presumably a slip of the tongue – the judge may not accept the speaker's claim of intended exception.

Key Terms
غير (ghayr): A word used as an adjective for indefinite nouns or as an exception, with original usage as adjective.
صفة (sifah): Adjective describing an indefinite noun, here affecting the scope of an acknowledgment.
استثناء (istithna): An exception that removes a part from the ruling, requiring accusative case for 'ghayr'.
تغليب (taghlib): Predominance: treating a word as belonging to a category (adverb) even when not strictly so, due to common usage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A dirham minus a daniq
C) Nothing
D) It depends on intention

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the same word can create different obligations depending on its grammatical function; ghayr's case ending is the decisive factor.

The Conditional Particle In: Its Definition and Conditions
Defining the conditional particle 'in' and its scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions for using the conditional particle 'in' in a conditional sentence and identify when an interpretation is required.

Core Idea
The conditional 'in' applies only to uncertain future possibilities, not to impossibilities or certainties.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding the precise use of conditional particles is crucial for correct interpretation of legal texts. This lesson examines the primary conditional particle 'in' (إن), which is reserved for pure condition on uncertain matters. We will explore its definition, its conditions, and a key fiqh illustration involving divorce.

Guided Path
1
State the definition of 'in' as the original conditional particle
The passage asserts that 'in' is the primary particle because it is used exclusively for pure condition, unlike other particles used for other meanings.
2
Identify the condition for its correct usage
It applies only to a non-existent matter that is at risk of existence (معدوم على خطر الوجود), i.e., uncertain future possibility.
3
Distinguish cases requiring interpretation
For impossible or necessarily existent matters, 'in' cannot be used without some interpretation; those are domains of 'law' and 'idha' respectively.
4
Apply the condition to the divorce example
The husband's condition 'If I do not divorce you...' is valid because the non-divorce is uncertain until death; the divorce triggers only at the approach of death.
5
Analyze the fiqh ruling on inheritance
The passage distinguishes between consummated and non-consummated marriages for the fleeing woman (imra'at al-farr), showing how the ruling is derived from the condition's verification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و"إن" أصل فيها؛ لأنها لم تستعمل إلا لهذا المعنى، وغيرها تستعمل لمعان أخر، ولهذا غلب "إن" فسمي الكل بحرف الشرط وإن كان بعضها اسما. كإذا أي لكون أن الأصل وإنما تدخل على أمر معدوم على خطر الوجود وليس بكائن لا محالة، فلا تستعمل فيما لم يكن على خطر الوجود بل محالاً إلا بضرب من التأويل؛ لأنه محل "لو"، ولا يستعمل على أمر كائن لا محالة إلا بالتأويل؛ لأنه محل إذا. فإذا قال: "إن لم أطلقك فأنت طالق" لم تطلق حتى يموت أحدهما؛ لأن هذا الشرط. الزوج لزوجته أي عدم التطليق لا يعلم قطعًا إلا حين موت أحدهما، فإنه قبل الموت يمكن في كل حين أن يطلقها فإذا لم يطلق وشارف موت الزوج تطلق وتحرم عن الميراث إن كانت غير مدخول بها، بخلاف ما إذا كانت مدخولاً بها؛ لأن امرأة الفار ترث بعد الدخول، وكذا إذا شارف موت المرأة تطلق ألبتة؛ لأنه تحقق الشرط حينئذ.
And 'in' is the original (primary) among them; because it is not used except for this meaning, while others are used for other meanings. For this reason 'in' predominates, and all are called conditional particles, even if some are nouns. Like 'idha' because it is original. And it only applies to a non-existent matter that is at risk of existence and not necessarily existent. So it is not used for something that is not at risk of existence, rather impossible, except with a certain interpretation; because that is the domain of 'law' (if). And it is not used for something necessarily existent except with interpretation; because that is the domain of 'idha' (when). So if he (a husband) says to his wife: 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced,' she is not divorced until one of them dies; because this condition (the husband not having divorced) is not known with certainty except at the time of one's death. For before death, it is possible at every moment that he divorces her. So if he does not divorce and the husband's death approaches, she becomes divorced and is prohibited from inheritance if she is not yet consummated, contrary to if she has been consummated; because the fleeing woman's wife inherits after consummation. Similarly, if the wife's death approaches, she becomes divorced immediately because the condition is then realized.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage explains the conditional particle 'إن' (in), asserting that it is the original particle for pure condition because it is exclusively used for that meaning, unlike other conditional tools that may have other uses. 'إن' only applies to a future, non-existent matter that is possible to occur (على خطر الوجود) – something that may or may not happen. It cannot be used for impossible matters (e.g., 'if the sun rises from the west') without a special interpretation, nor for certain occurrences (e.g., 'if the sun rises') without interpretation. The example from Hanafi fiqh: a husband says 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced.' This is valid only when the condition (his not divorcing her) is uncertain. Since he might divorce her at any time, the condition becomes known only at the death of one spouse. At that point, if he has not divorced her before death, the divorce takes effect. There is a significant fiqh ruling regarding 'الفرار' (fleeing) – if a man divorces his wife during a fatal illness to deprive her of inheritance, the divorced wife inherits if consummation occurred. Here, the divorce occurring at the approach of death triggers the same ruling, so the wife inherits if she was consummated, but if not, she does not inherit.

Key Terms
إن (in): The primary conditional particle used only for pure condition, applying to uncertain future events.
خطر الوجود (khatr al-wujud): A state where something is non-existent but its existence is possible and uncertain.
امرأة الفار (imra'at al-farr): A woman whose husband divorces her during a fatal illness to exclude her from inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can the particle 'إن' (in) be used in a conditional sentence according to this passage?
A) For any future event
B) Only for impossible events
C) For a non-existent matter at risk of existence
D) For events that are certain to occur

Key Takeaway
The conditional particle 'in' in Hanafi usul is restricted to uncertain future possibilities and cannot be applied to impossibilities or certainties without interpretation.

The Conditional Particle 'Idha' in Talaq: A Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Textual analysis of the conditional particle 'idha' and its legal effect in divorce statements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Sahibayn positions on the particle 'idha' in conditional talaq and apply the Hanafi principle of doubt (shakk) to prevent immediate occurrence.

Core Idea
Idha in talaq: Abu Hanifa treats it as pure condition; the Sahibayn as temporal — and doubt blocks immediate divorce.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar analyses the Arabic conditional particle 'idha' in a classic divorce formulation. The disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hinges on whether 'idha' retains its temporal sense or becomes a pure conditional. The resolution involves the principle of doubt (shakk) and the role of intention. You will learn how a single word choice can change the timing of a legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed utterance
The husband says: 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced' (إذا لم أطلقك فأنت طالق). The key is the particle 'idha'.
2
State Abu Hanifa's interpretation
Abu Hanifa sees 'idha' as a pure conditional (like 'in'), losing temporal meaning. Thus the condition is not fulfilled until death.
3
State the Sahibayn's interpretation
The Sahibayn hold 'idha' retains temporal meaning, so the condition is fulfilled immediately after the utterance, triggering instant talaq.
4
Analyse the rebuttal
The Hanafi rebuttal uses the example 'idha shi'ta' (whenever you wish) to show 'idha' does not always indicate time, and the principle of doubt (shakk) blocks immediate occurrence.
5
Note the role of intention
If the husband intended a specific meaning (time or condition), that intention is followed. The particle 'idha ma' is agreed to indicate requital.

Source Text

وهذا كله إذا لم ينو شيئًا أما إذا نوى الوقت أو الشرط فهو على ما نوى.
و"إذا ما" مثل "إذا لكنه لم ينفك عنه معنى المجازاة بالاتفاق.
Explanation of the third division. Discussion of 'idha'. The condition is necessarily implied without intention, like the subject implying the meaning of condition. So if a man says to his wife: 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced', divorce does not occur according to him (Abu Hanifa) unless one of them dies, because in his view it is like a conditional particle, and the meaning of time has been dropped, so it becomes as if he said: 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced', and in that case it does not occur until one dies. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: it occurs immediately after he finishes, like 'when I do not divorce you', because in their view the meaning of time is not removed, so the meaning becomes: in a time when I do not divorce you, you are divorced. So when he finishes speaking, there is a time in which he did not divorce her, so it occurs immediately, as in 'mata'. And the evidence for this is that if he said: 'You are divorced whenever you wish', it is not restricted to the gathering like 'whenever you wish'. The answer is that divorce is attached to the will, so doubt arises about its termination... so it does not terminate. And in our case, doubt arises about immediate occurrence, so it does not occur due to doubt. (Glosses: 'Tadamman' means the utterance restricts the fulfillment of one clause to the fulfillment of another, and the combination of literal and metaphorical is only impossible if intended, etc. 'From the beginning without intention' etc. The combination of literal and metaphorical is impossible if the metaphor is intended, but here it is not. 'Like the subject implying etc.' like 'whoever comes to me, for him is a dirham'. 'And in it' i.e. in his statement 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced'. 'And the two said etc.' The author of al-Muslim says: a rebuttal against them: if he intended pure condition, the qadi should not accept his intention because it contradicts the apparent meaning, though it is accepted by agreement if he intended it; the dispute is only when there is no intention, so ponder. 'As soon as he finishes' i.e. from this statement. 'And the kaaf in kama faragha is for suddenness not simile, as in 'as I went out I saw Zayd' i.e. I was surprised at the moment of going out at the moment of seeing Zayd. 'And the evidence for this' i.e. that the word 'idha' does not lose the meaning of time as they said. 'Does not restrict' etc. so if she wills after that gathering she is divorced, thus it is known that 'idha' is for general time. 'The attachment of divorce to will' etc. if 'idha' is interpreted as 'the cutting of attachment to will', then his statement 'you are divorced if you wish' would be restricted to the gathering, and if 'idha' is interpreted as 'mata' it would not terminate, and there is no doubt that it is attached in the present, so doubt arises in its termination, i.e. in the termination of attachment, for the original in attachment is continuity, so it does not terminate. 'And in our case' i.e. in his statement 'if I do not divorce you, you are divorced', doubt arises about immediate occurrence; if 'idha' is interpreted as condition meaning the divorce does not occur until one of them dies, and if interpreted as time, divorce occurs immediately after finishing this statement, so it does not occur due to doubt. All this is if he did not intend anything. But if he intended time or condition, it is according to his intention. And 'idha ma' is like 'idha', but the meaning of requital is not separated from it by agreement.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the Arabic conditional particle 'idha' in the context of divorce (talaq). The author presents the classical Hanafi position of Imam Abu Hanifa against the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad). The ruling concerns a husband who says to his wife: 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced.' Abu Hanifa holds that the word 'idha' here functions purely as a conditional particle, like 'in', and loses its temporal sense. Therefore, the divorce is not effective until one of the spouses dies, because the condition ('if I do not divorce you') is not fulfilled until death. The Sahibayn argue that 'idha' retains its original temporal meaning, indicating a time in which the condition is met. Thus, as soon as the husband finishes speaking, there exists a time when he has not divorced her, so the divorce takes effect immediately. They support this by analogy with the word 'mata' (whenever), which triggers immediate effect. The Hanafi rebuttal uses another example: if the husband says 'You are divorced whenever you wish' (idha shi'ta), the wife's choice is not limited to the immediate gathering, contrary to the word 'mata shi'ta'. This shows that 'idha' is not purely temporal. The author concludes that due to the doubt (shakk) about immediate occurrence, the divorce is not effective immediately. Furthermore, if the husband had a specific intention (time or condition), that intention is followed. The particle 'idha ma' is similar to 'idha' but, by consensus, always retains the meaning of requital (jazā'), which is a nuance.

Key Terms
إذا (idha): A conditional particle that, according to Abu Hanifa, functions purely as a conditional (like 'in') losing its temporal meaning; according to Sahibayn, it retains its temporal meaning and indicates a time.
متى (mata): A conditional particle meaning 'whenever', which according to Sahibayn is analogous to 'idha' in retaining temporal meaning and causing immediate effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to his wife 'إذا لم أطلقك فأنت طالق' (If I do not divorce you, you are divorced), when does the divorce occur according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Immediately after the utterance.
B) After one lunar month.
C) Not until one of the spouses dies.
D) When the wife demands it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the particle 'idha' is interpreted as a pure conditional by Abu Hanifa, delaying talaq until death, due to doubt about immediate occurrence.

Delegating Divorce to Wife’s Wish: The Effects of ‘كيف’ and ‘كم’ in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Intra-Hanafi dispute over root and attribute in divorce delegation using 'كيف' and 'كم'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the effect of delegating divorce using ‘كيف’ and ‘كم’, and derive the ruling for a consummated wife based on each view.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, the root of divorce (asl) and its attribute (wasf) are treated differently: Abu Hanifa separates them; the Sahibayn treat them equally, suspending the entire divorce on the wife's wish.

This lesson dissects the Hanafi usul analysis of two key words used in divorce delegation: 'كيف' (how) and 'كم' (how many). The passage presents a classic intra-madhhab disagreement: does the root of divorce (the dissolution itself) fall immediately, or is it suspended on the wife's wish as part of the delegated attribute? Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply usul principles—like the distinction between material and non-material matters and the role of linguistic ambiguity—to real cases of legal delegation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the delegation scenario and the operative words
The husband says 'أنت طالق كيف شئت' (you are divorced as you wish) or 'أنت طالق كم شئت' (you are divorced however many you wish). The word 'كيف' refers to the manner/quality (e.g., revocable or irrevocable) and implicitly the number; 'كم' explicitly asks for the number. Note that the husband delegates part of the divorce attributes to the wife's choice.
The case assumes a consummated wife unless stated otherwise.
2
Distinguish between root (asl) and attribute (wasf) in divorce
In Hanafi usul, the divorce itself is the root (asl) – the legal dissolution of marriage. The quality (type, number) is the attribute (wasf). The debate centers on whether the root can exist without a specific attribute, and whether attributing the attribute to the wife's wish necessarily also attributes the root.
Abu Hanifa sees them as separable; the Sahibayn see them as inseparable in non-material legal matters.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa: For a consummated wife, one revocable divorce falls immediately; the wife's wish only determines the attribute (e.g., whether it becomes irrevocable or triples). For a non-consummated wife, one irrevocable divorce falls immediately regardless of her wish. Proof: The root is fundamental and does not depend on the attribute; the word 'كيف' is ambiguous but defaults to one revocable. The Sahibayn: For all non-material matters (like divorce and manumission), the root and attribute are equal because both are non-material. Therefore, if the attribute is attached to her wish, the root must also be attached; no divorce occurs until she wishes. They argue that it is impossible to have a divorce without a quality (e.g., it must be revocable or irrevocable), so the root cannot exist independently.
The difference turns on whether non-material matters are analogized to material substances or to accidents.
4
Apply the ruling to consummated vs. non-consummated wife
For a consummated wife: Abu Hanifa says one revocable divorce falls immediately, and her wish affects only the type/number. The Sahibayn say she remains married until she wishes, and then the divorce occurs as she wishes. For a non-consummated wife: Both agree that one irrevocable divorce falls immediately, and the delegation is void (no benefit).
The non-consummated case is simpler because the wife cannot have two separate waiting periods.
5
Analyze the word 'كم' and the super-commentator's inclination
If the husband says 'أنت طالق كم شئت', the Sahibayn say she does not get divorced until she wishes, because 'كم' refers to a number that exists externally; here no number exists externally, so all numbers are suspended. The super-commentator (Bahr al-Ulum) inclines toward the Sahibayn's view for both 'كيف' and 'كم', considering their position more consistent with the non-material nature of divorce. However, the well-known position of the school (zahir al-riwaya) is Abu Hanifa's view for 'كيف' and the Sahibayn's for 'كم'.
The text presents the Sahibayn's view as more logically sound for non-material matters.

Source Text

بحث "كيف" بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث فإن نوت الثنتين ونواهما أيضًا لا يقع؛ لأنّه عدد محض ليس مدلولاً للفظ. وأما الثلاث فإنه وإن لم يكن أيضًا مدلول اللفظ لكنه واحد اعتباري بما احتمله اللفظ، عند وجود الدليل ههنا هو لفظ "كيف"، وإنما احتاج إلى موافقة نية الزوج مع أنه فوّض الأحوال بيدها؛ لأنّ حالة مشيئتها مشتركة بين البينونة والعدد محتاجة إلى النية ليتعين أحد المرأة محتمليه. وهذا كلّه إذا كانت مدخولاً بها، فإن لم تكن مدخولاً بها تقع الواحدة، وتبين بها، ويلغو قوله: "كيف شئتِ"؛ لعدم الفائدة. وقالا ما لم يقبل الإشارة فحاله ووصفه بمنزلة أصله، فيتعلق الأصل بتعلقه، يعني أن أي بالمشيئة أي الوصف عندهما كلّ ما كان من الأمور الشرعية الغير المحسوسة كالطلاق والعتاق ونحوهما فالحال كالبيع والنكاح والأصل بمنزلة واحدة؛ إذهما غير محسوسين، فلا معنى لجعل أحدهما واقعا والآخر موقوفا، بل يعلّق الأصل بالمشيئة كما تعلق الوصف بها، فلا يقع ما لم تشأ؛ أي الطلاق واحد اعتباري فإنه واحد حكمي على ما مرّ فتذكر. (القمر) لأن حالة مشيئتها إلخ: يعني أن حال الطلاق فوضت إلى مشيئة المرأة بكلمة "كيف"، وهذه الحال تشترك بين البينونة والعدد؛ فيحتاج إلى نية الزوج لتعيين أحد المحتملين كذا قيل والمانع أن يمنع كون حال المشيئة مشتركة بل يقول: "إنّها مطلقة، وقد رأيت في نسخة مكتوبة بيد الشارح الله هكذا، لأنّ حاله مشتبه مشترك بين إلخ، وقال الطحاوي أبو بكر الرازي له: إن نية الزوج ليس شرطًا لها في أن تجعل الطلاق بائنا أو ثلاثًا في قول أبي حنيفة بالله. كذا نقل ابن الملك لله. (القمر) أحد محتمليه إلخ : فإذا كان نية الزوج في العدد فتعين أن مشيئتها في الصفة، وإذا كان نية الزوج في الصفة فتعيّن أن مشيئتها في العدد. (السنبلي) وهذا أي وقوع الواحدة وتفويض الأحوال والكيفيات إليها. (القمر) لعدم الفائدة: أي في التعليق على المشيئة لعدم المحل؛ فإنّ غير الموطوءة تبين بواحدة ولا عدة لها. (القمر) كالطلاق والعتاق: إيماء إلى أنّ خلاف الصاحبين في كلتا مسألتي الطلاق والعتاق لا في الطلاق فقط. (القمر) بمنزلة واحدة إلخ هذا الدليل غير تام؛ لأنّ مساواة الأصل والوصف في غير المحسوس مما لم يقم عليه دليل هذا، وهذا الدليل هو المشهور للإمام، وغير المشهور هو مذكور في "المسلم" وشرحه، فانظر هناك. (السنبلي) إذ هما: أي الحال لما لم يكن محسوساً كان معرفة وجوده بآثاره وأوصافه؛ فافتقرت حينئذ معرفة ثبوت الأصل إلى معرفة أثره ووصفه كثبوت الملك في البيع وثبوت الحلّ في النكاح والوصف أيضًا مفتقر إلى الأصل: فاستويا فلا معنى إلخ. (القمر) بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بحث "كيف" وذلك لئلا يلزم الترجيح بلا مرجّح لا لأنّ قيام العرض بالعرض ممتنع؛ فينبغي أن يقوما معا بالمحلّ على ما ظنوا وبنوا عليه النكات وبما حرّرنا اندفع ما قيل: إنّ في كلام المصنف مصر مسامحة القلب والأولى أن يقول : فأصله بمنزلة حاله ووصفه، فيتعلق الأصل بتعلّقه؛ وذلك لأنه إذا جعل الحال والأصل بمنزلة الشيء الواحد أخذ كلّ منها حكم الآخر. وأبو حنيفة حاله يقول : يلزم من هذا اتباع الأصل للوصف، وهو خلاف القياس فلا يعتبر. و"كم" اسم للعدد الواقع، فإذا قال: "أنت طالق كم شئت" لم تطلق ما لم تشأ؛ لأنه لمّا أي الاندفاع كان اسما للعدد الواقع الموجود في الخارج ولم يكن في الخارج ههنا عدد حتى يسأل عنه وذلك: أي تعلّق الأصل بالمشيئة بسبب تعلّق الوصف بها. (القمر) لا لأنّ قيام العرض إلخ: اعلم أن بعضهم بنوا قول الصاحبين على أن قيام العرض بالعرض ممتنع، فليس أنّ الطلاق أصل والكيفية عرض وحال قائم به، بل هما سِيّان؛ فيقومان معًا بالمحلّ. فإذا تعلّق أحدهما بمشيئتها تعلّق الآخر. ولمّا كان يرد عليه أن هذا مخالف لسوق كلامهم؛ فإنهم قالوا: حاله ووصفه بمنزلة أصله وهذا صريح في أن أحدهما أصل والآخر وصف وحال أعرض عنه الشارح وقال: لا لأنّ إلخ ثم اعلم أنه وقع في بعض نسخ الشرح لأن قيام العرض" إلخ. وصاحب مسير الدائر" وجد هذه النسخة ونقل عبارتها، ولا يخفى على اللبيب أنّ هذه النسخة لا معنى لها، فتدبر . (القمر) وبما حررنا أي من أنّ الأصل والحال مساويان (القمر) ما قيل: القائل صاحب "تعليق الأنوار شرح المنار".(القمر) والأولى إلخ لأنّ المنظور قياس الأصل على الحال والوصف. (القمر) من هذا: أي من تعلق الأصل بالمشيئة بسبب تعلّق الحال والوصف بها. (القمر) وهو خلاف القياس أقول: إنّ حالاً من أحوال الطلاق لازم له، والزوج علق جميع الأحوال على مشيئة الزوجة؛ فيتعلّق الطلاق أيضًا على مشيئتها. فلو وقع الطلاق بلا كيفية وحال فهو محال؛ لأنه يلزم انفكاك الملزوم عن اللازم، ولو وقع بكيفية فهو مخالف لقول الزوج؛ لأنه علّق جميع الأحوال على المشيئة، فلا جَرَم لا يقع الطلاق أيضا بدون المشيئة، وتبعية الأصل للازمه في التعلّق ليس بخلاف القياس، بل هو عين المعقول، فالأشبه قول الصاحبين رحمها كذا قال بحر العلوم مولانا عبد العلي يه. (القمر) للعدد الواقع إلخ: أورد أن "كم" اسم للعدد وقع أو لم يقع؛ فلا معنى لتقييد العدد بالواقع وإرادة الموجود في الخارج من الواقع والأحسن في توجيه عبارة المتن أن يقال: إن "كم" اسم اسم للعدد الواقع أي العدد الذي من أن يقع، فإذا قال: "أنت طالق كم شئت" لم تطلق ما لم تشأ؛ لأنه علق جميع الأعداد بمشيئتها، وإنما يصير جميع الأعداد معلقًا بمشيئتها إذا تعلّق أصل الطلاق بها؛ فلا يقع دونها، فتأمل. (القمر) فتأمل.(القمر) شأنه
Section on 'how': Explanation of the divisions of the third division. If she intends two divorces and both are intended [by the husband], it does not occur because it is pure number not indicated by the wording. As for three, although it is also not indicated by the wording, it is a considered single unit because the wording admits it, when there exists an indication here which is the word 'how'. He needed the agreement of the husband's intention despite the fact that he delegated the situations to her hand, because the state of her wish is shared between irrevocable divorce and number, needing intention to specify one of the two probable meanings. All this if she is entered upon; if she is not entered upon, one divorce occurs and she becomes separated by it, and his saying 'as you wish' is void due to lack of benefit. And they two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: as long as it does not accept indication, its condition and attribute are like its root, so the root is attached to its attachment. That is, by the wish, i.e., the attribute: according to them, everything from non-material legal matters such as divorce and manumission and the like, the condition and the root are of one status because they are non-material, so there is no meaning to making one actual and the other suspended, rather the root is attached to the wish just as the attribute is attached to it, so it does not occur until she wishes. The divorce is a considered single unit, so it is a legal single unit as previously mentioned, so remember. (al-Qamar) 'Because her state of wish etc.': means that the state of divorce was delegated to the woman's wish by the word 'how', and this state is shared between irrevocable divorce and number; so it needs the husband's intention to specify one of the two probabilities. This is as said, and the preventer can prevent that the state of wish is shared, rather he says: 'she is divorced, and I have seen in a copy written by the commentator's hand, God, thus: because its state is ambiguous, shared between etc.' And al-Tahawi Abu Bakr al-Razi said to him: The husband's intention is not a condition for her to make the divorce irrevocable or triple in the opinion of Abu Hanifa, by God. Thus transmitted by Ibn al-Malik for God. (al-Qamar) 'One of its probabilities etc.': So if the husband's intention is regarding number, then it is determined that her wish is regarding the attribute; if the husband's intention is regarding the attribute, then it is determined that her wish is regarding the number. (al-Sunbuli) And this is the occurrence of one divorce and the delegation of the states and qualities to her. (al-Qamar) 'Due to lack of benefit': i.e., in suspending upon the wish because of lack of subject; for the non-consummated woman becomes separated by one divorce and has no waiting period. (al-Qamar) 'Like divorce and manumission': an indication that the difference of the two companions is in both matters of divorce and manumission, not only in divorce. (al-Qamar) 'Of one status etc.': This proof is incomplete because the equality of root and attribute in non-material matters has no proof. This proof is the well-known one for the Imam, and the lesser-known one is mentioned in 'al-Muslim' and its commentary, so look there. (al-Sunbuli) 'Since they both': i.e., since the condition was not sensible, knowing its existence was through its effects and descriptions; so then knowing the establishment of the root became dependent on knowing its effect and description, like the establishment of ownership in sale and the establishment of permissibility in marriage, and the description is also dependent on the root; so they are equal, so there is no meaning etc. (al-Qamar) Explanation of the divisions of the third division: section on 'how': and that is to avoid preference without a preponderance, not because the existence of an accident on an accident is impossible; so they should both exist together in the subject as they thought and built upon it the fine points. And by what we have written is refuted what was said: 'In the author's speech there is a place of leniency, and it would be better for him to say: so its root is like its condition and attribute, so the root is attached to its attachment; because if he makes the condition and the root like one thing, each takes the ruling of the other.' And Abu Hanifa says: it follows from this the root's following the attribute, which is contrary to analogy, so it is not considered. And 'how many' is a noun for actual number; so if he says: 'you are divorced however many you wish' she is not divorced until she wishes, because it was a noun for actual number that exists externally, and here there is no number externally to be asked about. That is, the attachment of the root to the wish due to the attachment of the attribute to it. (al-Qamar) 'Not because existence of accident etc.': Know that some built the saying of the two companions on the impossibility of an accident subsisting in an accident; so it is not that divorce is a root and the quality is an accident and condition subsisting in it, but rather they are equal; so they both subsist together in the subject. So if one of them is attached to her wish, the other is also attached. And when it is objected that this contradicts the flow of their speech; for they said: its condition and attribute are like its root, and this is explicit that one is root and the other is attribute and condition; the commentator turned away from it and said 'not because...' etc. Then know that in some copies of the commentary it says 'because existence of accident' etc. And the author of 'Musir al-Da'ir' found this copy and transmitted its wording; and it is not hidden from the intelligent that this copy has no meaning, so reflect. (al-Qamar) 'And by what we have written': i.e., that the root and condition are equal (al-Qamar) 'What was said': the speaker is the author of 'Ta'liq al-Anwar Sharh al-Manar' (al-Qamar) 'And it would be better etc.': because the perspective is analogizing the root to the condition and attribute. (al-Qamar) 'From this': i.e., from the attachment of the root to the wish due to the attachment of the condition and attribute to it. (al-Qamar) 'And it is contrary to analogy': I say: a condition from the conditions of divorce is necessary for it, and the husband attached all conditions to the wife's wish; so divorce also becomes attached to her wish. If divorce occurs without a quality and condition, it is impossible because it would entail the separation of the determined from its necessary companion; and if it occurs with a quality, it contradicts the husband's saying because he attached all conditions to the wish; so inevitably divorce also does not occur without the wish. The dependence of the root on its necessary companion in attachment is not contrary to analogy; rather it is the essence of reason. So the saying of the two companions, may God have mercy on them, is more appropriate. Thus said Bahr al-Ulum Mawlana Abd al-Ali. (al-Qamar) 'For actual number etc.': It is objected that 'how many' is a noun for number whether actual or not; so there is no meaning to restricting number to actual and intending what exists externally. The best in directing the text's wording is to say: ''how many' is a noun for number that is about to occur, so if he says 'you are divorced however many you wish' she is not divorced until she wishes; because he attached all numbers to her wish, and all numbers become attached to her wish only if the root of divorce is attached to it; so it does not occur without it, so reflect.' (al-Qamar) 'So reflect.' (al-Qamar) 'Its nature.'
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the word 'كيف' (how) and 'كم' (how many) when used by a husband in delegating divorce to his wife's wish. The author, from the Hanafi usul tradition, explains the rulings and the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

The core scenario: a husband says to his wife 'أنت طالق كيف شئت' (you are divorced as you wish). This delegates the authority to the wife to choose the manner (state) and number of divorce. The text first discusses the case of a consummated wife. If the husband intends a specific number (e.g., two or three) in his heart, that intention is considered alongside the wife's wish. For two divorces, since two is a pure number not indicated by the word 'كيف', it does not fall unless the wife wishes three; but if the husband intended three, the wording 'كيف' can potentially bear three as a single considered unit, so with evidence (the word 'كيف') it may fall as three if the wife wishes. However, the husband's intention is needed to specify whether the delegation covers the number or the type, because the word 'كيف' is ambiguous between irrevocable divorce (a state) and number. If the wife is not consummated, only one divorce occurs immediately regardless of her wish, and the husband's delegation is void because there is no benefit (no iddah or further divorce needed).

The Sahibayn hold a different principle: for non-material legal matters like divorce and manumission, the 'root' (the divorce itself) and its 'attribute' (the quality or number) are equal in status because both are non-material. Therefore, if the husband attaches the attribute to the wife's wish (by saying 'كيف شئت'), the root (the divorce) is also attached to her wish; it does not occur until she wishes. They argue that it is impossible to consider one as actual and the other as pending without a preponderator. Abu Hanifa disagrees, arguing that the root should not follow the attribute because that would be contrary to analogy (qiyas). The root is fundamental, and the attribute is a description of it; in material things, the attribute cannot exist without the root, but here the root can exist without a specific attribute (e.g., one revocable divorce). Therefore, the root falls immediately as one revocable divorce, and only the attribute (the type or number) is delegated to her wish.

The passage also discusses the word 'كم' (how many). If the husband says 'أنت طالق كم شئت' (you are divorced however many you wish), the Sahibayn say it does not fall until she wishes, because 'كم' refers to a specific number that exists externally, but here no number exists yet. Abu Hanifa would likely apply similar reasoning: the root divorce falls immediately as one, and the number is delegated. However, the text seems to side with the Sahibayn's view on 'كم', noting that all numbers are attached to her wish only if the root is attached, so the divorce does not occur without her wish.

Overall, this passage showcases Hanafi usul methodology: analyzing the linguistic implications of words ('كيف' as ambiguous, 'كم' as a noun for number), applying principles of causality (illa), and addressing inter-madhhab disagreement (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) with rational proofs.

Key Terms
كيف (kayfa): An interrogative word meaning 'how'; used in divorce delegation to refer to the manner or quality of divorce (e.g., revocable, irrevocable) and by implication the number.
حال (haal): The state or condition of the divorce (e.g., bainuna or number), which is delegated to the wife's wish.
أصل (asl): The root or essence of the divorce, i.e., the legal dissolution of marriage itself.
وصف (wasf): The attribute or quality of the divorce, such as being one, two, three, revocable, or irrevocable.
كم (kam): Interrogative meaning 'how many'; a noun referring to the number of divorces that are to occur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his consummated wife 'أنت طالق كيف شئت' and intends (in his heart) that she should choose the number of divorces, according to Abu Hanifa, what is the default ruling?
A) No divorce falls until she wishes and specifies the number.
B) One revocable divorce falls immediately, and her wish determines whether it becomes additional divorces.
C) Three divorces fall immediately regardless of her wish.
D) The divorce is suspended entirely on her wish, and she can decide both number and type.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the root of divorce (asl) and its attribute (wasf) are treated differently by Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn; the school's mufta bihi applies Abu Hanifa's view for 'كيف' (immediate divorce) and the Sahibayn's view for 'كم' (suspensed).
